        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;

        }

        }

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





mmap$drm_gem_mmap will call *drm_gem_mmap_obj*[1] to map a GEM object. *drm_gem_mmap_obj* will set *obj* to *vma->vm_private_data*[2], and call mmap function pointer via *obj->funcs->mmap*[3]. If it is a *drm_gem_cma_object*, it will call *drm_gem_cma_object_mmap* which just calls *drm_gem_cma_mmap*. If *dma_mmap_pages* or *dma_mmap_wc* failed, it will call *drm_gem_vm_close*[4] to close the vma. It just calls *drm_gem_object_put*[5] to decrese the reference of *vma->vm_private_data*. And finally it will go the error path in *drm_gem_mmap_obj*, call *drm_gem_object_put*[6] again. So it will decrease the reference twice, leading to uaf.



<span class="line"><!---->mmap$drm_gem_mmap will call *drm_gem_mmap_obj*[1] to map a GEM object. *drm_gem_mmap_obj* will set *obj* to *vma-&gt;vm_private_data*[2], and call mmap function pointer via *obj-&gt;funcs-&gt;mmap*[3]. If it is a *drm_gem_cma_object*, it will call *drm_gem_cma_object_mmap* which just calls *drm_gem_cma_mmap*. If *dma_mmap_pages* or *dma_mmap_wc* failed, it will call *drm_gem_vm_close*[4] to close the vma. It just calls *drm_gem_object_put*[5] to decrese the reference of *vma-&gt;vm_private_data*. And finally it will go the error path in *drm_gem_mmap_obj*, call *drm_gem_object_put*[6] again. So it will decrease the reference twice, leading to uaf.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->1. Compile poc.<!----></span>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->2. Run poc in ChromiumOS system. (please make sure current user is in video group. it needs the privilege to access drm to trigger this bug).<!----></span>

, I don't doubt it is built into the kernel.. just that I don't see any driver that probes using it.  The gem cma helpers (more recently renamed to gem dma helpers) are mostly used by simple kms-only driver (and mostly things without iommu support but they could be used by drivers using the dma-api in front of an iommu).  The only thing in current chomebooks which fits that description would be mtk, but at least in upstream kernel it hasn't been converted over to use these helpers.



<span class="line"><!---->, I don't doubt it is built into the kernel.. just that I don't see any driver that probes using it. mediatek is enabled but does not use the CMA helpers.. however it had a similar issue for which I posted a patch[1], along with a couple other drivers.  (Rockchip may still be getting updates, I need to check.. exynos is not getting updates but I noticed it had the same issue so I posted a patch for upstream.)



<span class="line"><!---->mediatek is enabled but does not use the CMA helpers.. however it had a similar issue for which I posted a patch[1], along with a couple other drivers.  (Rockchip may still be getting updates, I need to check.. exynos is not getting updates but I noticed it had the same issue so I posted a patch for upstream.)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In any case, I'm not sure if userspace could manage to trigger this error path, it would require triggering dma_map_* to return an error or similar.



<span class="line"><!---->In any case, I'm not sure if userspace could manage to trigger this error path, it would require triggering dma_map_* to return an error or similar.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.



<span class="line"><!---->Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.<!----></span>
